A) The meaning of the waw (order vs. association).
B) The nature of 'atf (conjunction) and the conditional attachment.
C) The validity of the divorce for a non-consummated wife.
D) The number of divorces allowed in one session.

Key Takeaway
The dispute on the waw in conditional divorce is not about its lexical meaning but about the mechanism of conjunctive attachment in conditional sentences.

The Waw in Conditional Statements: Hal vs. Athf
Analyzing the waw in 'Tallaqni wa laki alf' and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible meanings of the waw (hal vs. athf) in conditional statements and apply the Hanafi principle of prioritizing haqiqah over majaz to determine the legal ruling.

Core Idea
The default waw is simple conjunction unless context forces simultaneity; the literal meaning prevails over custom.

This lesson delves into a classic usul al-fiqh debate: the interpretation of the Arabic particle waw in conditional phrases like 'Tallaqni wa laki alf'. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, insists on applying the literal meaning (haqiqah) of conjunction, while the Sahibayn invoke custom (urf) to read it as circumstantial (hal). Understanding this dispute trains you in the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible meanings of waw
Recognize that waw can function as simple conjunction (athf) or circumstantial accusative (hal), leading to different legal consequences.
2
Analyze the phrase structure
Examine the two clauses: one is imperative/performative, the other is declarative or performative. Determine if conjunction is grammatically possible.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of haqiqah
Prioritize the literal meaning (athf) unless a clear obstacle (like impossibility of conjunction) forces a metaphorical reading (hal).
4
Consider custom (urf) as a potential indicator
Evaluate whether customary usage in similar transactional contexts (e.g., khul') can override the literal meaning.
5
Derive the legal ruling
Based on the interpretation, state the consequence: if athf, the second clause is a promise; if hal, it is a condition for exchange.

According to him (Abu Hanifa) it is for conjunction, and his saying 'and you have a thousand' is a promise, so the wealth is not obligatory upon the husband's divorce; rather she must fulfill her promise religiously. It is interpreted as conjunction (giving priority to the literal) over the metaphorical, even if customary. The circumstantial meaning is only determined when exchange is necessary, and exchange is not necessary because divorce does not require consideration (unlike lease where exchange is necessary, so the circumstantial meaning is determined, like 'Carry it and you have a dirham'). This and the difference between the case of divorce and emancipation is problematic: in it they interpreted for the circumstantial case due to disjunction and left the literal conjunction, while disjunction is also realized here because 'Divorce me' is a demanding performative sentence and 'you have a thousand' is informative, as was in emancipation; custom also does not differ in understanding exchange. Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal analysis of the Arabic particle waw (واو) when used in conditional or contractual statements. It addresses two main scenarios: (1) the phrase 'Pay me a thousand and you are free' and (2) the phrase 'Divorce me and you have a thousand'. The central question is whether the waw indicates simultaneity (hal) or simple conjunction (athf). In the first scenario, the author explains that the waw must indicate hal because conjunction is impossible due to the disjunction between a performative demand and an informative statement. Thus, freedom is contingent on payment. However, there is a debate: some argue for inversion (qalb) to tie freedom to payment, while others say freedom is regarded as preceding but not actual. The preferred view is that freedom does not occur before payment. In the second scenario, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) interpret the waw as hal, making the thousand obligatory upon divorce as part of khul', while Abu Hanifa interprets it as conjunction, making it a non-binding promise. The passage contrasts this with ijarah (lease) where exchange is necessary, so the waw must be hal. The author notes the difficulty in distinguishing between divorce and emancipation cases. This analysis demonstrates how linguistic principles (haqiqah vs. majaz, custom, and the nature of sentences) directly affect legal rulings.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic particle for conjunction; can indicate simultaneity (hal) or simple conjunction (athf) depending on context.
الحال (al-hal): A circumstantial accusative indicating the state of the subject at the time of the action; here it refers to the waw indicating simultaneity.
العطف (al-athf): Conjunction; joining two elements without implying simultaneity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The wife is not obligated to pay the thousand.
D) The wife must pay after the husband's death.

Key Takeaway
The default waw is simple conjunction; custom can shift it to hal only when exchange is inherent, as in ijarah.

Thumma: Delay in Speech, Not in Legal Effect
Explaining thumma for delay and its application in divorce and conditional statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that thumma indicates delay in speech but not in legal effect to both unconditional and conditional divorce statements, and determine the number of divorces that occur.

Core Idea
Thumma delays speech, not rulings: all performative effects are immediate.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the particle thumma (ثم) literally means 'then' with a temporal gap. But when used in a performative statement like divorce, the legal effect must be instantaneous—otherwise, the ruling would lag behind the utterance, which is impossible. This lesson explores how Abu Hanifa reconciled thumma's literal meaning with the nature of injunctions, and how this applies to serial divorce statements and conditional divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal meaning of thumma
Thumma indicates a delay (tarakhi) with a pause between two events. It is used for sequential ordering, as in the example of praising the Prophet and then the Companions in descending rank.
In Arabic, thumma implies a temporal gap, unlike wa (و) which implies simultaneity or mere sequence.
2
Understand the nature of performatives
A performative (insha') creates its legal effect instantly upon utterance. The ruling cannot be delayed; otherwise, the performative would be detached from its effect, which is a logical impossibility (khalf).
Hanafi usul holds that the ruling of a performative is inherently immediate (munajjaz).
3
Apply to unconditional divorce for a consummated wife
If a husband says to his consummated wife 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', all three divorces occur at once. The thumma only indicates a pause in speech, not a delay in the legal effect.
For a consummated wife (al-madkhul biha), three divorces in one session count as three, making her irrevocably divorced (ba'in).
4
Apply to conditional divorce for a non-consummated wife
In a conditional statement like 'If you enter, (you are) divorced, then divorced, then divorced', the condition only attaches to the immediately adjacent first divorce. The second divorce occurs immediately (unconditionally) and the third is invalid (لغو).
For a non-consummated wife, three divorces are not possible; the third is void because only one revocable divorce is allowed before separation.
5
Analyze the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi tarjih
Some scholars might argue that thumma delays the legal effect itself, but Abu Hanifa (and the Hanafi school) insists that the delay is only in the pronunciation, not in the consequence. The tarjih is based on the principle that the ruling of a performative cannot lag.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that in the unconditional case, all three count; in the conditional case, only the first is conditioned.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Issue: (Issue: Thumma is for delay in the ruling with a pause. And thumma comes for the descending rank) as is said: May Allah bless Muhammad, then Abu Bakr, then Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, may Allah be pleased with them. And it is common in moving from one topic to another. They said: All three occur immediately together in the case of the consummated wife in his saying 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced' because the ruling of a performative does not lag behind it; if delay and pause were considered here, it would entail the ruling lagging behind the immediate performative, which is a violation. So the pause is nullified. But Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, considered the delay in speaking regarding the word thumma, as if he first spoke the first conjunct, then paused, then spoke what is after thumma, and so on. If it is conditioned by a condition placed (before) the dependent (or after), then the condition is not truly attached except to the immediately adjacent one. So if he says to a non-consummated wife: 'If you enter, (you are) divorced, then divorced, then divorced', the first is attached to the condition, the second falls immediately, and the third is invalid. And in delaying the condition, the first falls immediately and the last two are invalid. And if he says to a consummated wife, (the ruling) occurs...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage discusses the particle thumma (ثم) and its meaning of delay (tarakhi) with a pause between events. In legal contexts, thumma creates a temporal gap. However, when used in performative statements like divorce, the effect of the divorce cannot be delayed because performatives are inherently instantaneous. Therefore, in a statement like 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced' to a consummated wife, all three divorces occur at once, because considering the delay would contradict the nature of the performative. Abu Hanifa reconciles this by saying that the delay pertains to the speaking itself, not the legal effect: the speaker says the first, pauses, then says the second, etc. But the legal effect is still immediate for each utterance. In conditional sentences with thumma, the condition only attaches to the immediately adjacent clause. For example, if a non-consummated wife is told 'If you enter, (you are) divorced, then divorced, then divorced', the first divorce is conditioned on entry, the second occurs immediately (unconditionally), and the third is invalid. The passage ends with the beginning of the case for a consummated wife, which is cut off.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating delay (tarakhi) with a pause; used for sequential ordering with a temporal gap.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): Delay; the meaning of thumma that there is a gap between events.
المدخول بها (al-madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce.
B) Two divorces.
C) Three divorces immediately.
D) Three divorces with delays between them.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, thumma delays speech, not legal effect; thus, all performative consequences are immediate, and in conditional statements, the condition attaches only to the adjacent clause.

Fa' for Causality and Its Legal Implications
Explaining the use of fa' for causality and its effect on suspended talaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that fa' imposes order in suspended talaq to determine the number of divorces, and distinguish between the uses of fa' for causality (ta'lil) and sequence (ta'qib).

Core Idea
Fa' in suspended talaq imposes order: only one divorce occurs if multiple are linked by fa'.

In this lesson, we examine the linguistic particle fa' and its dual role as an indicator of both sequence and causality. The passage focuses on a key Hanafi rule: when fa' is used to conjoin suspended divorces, it imposes a logical order, resulting in only one divorce being effective. This contrasts with the conjunction waw, which would make all three occur simultaneously. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying usul al-fiqh to conditional talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic functions of fa'
The passage states that fa' is used both for sequence (ta'qib) and causality (ta'lil). Examples: 'Pay, for you are free' (fa' indicates causality). Identify how fa' connects the action to its reason.
Causality means the preceding clause is the cause of the following.
2
Apply fa' to suspended talaq
Consider the conditional: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced (fa-taliq) divorced (fa-taliq) divorced (fa-taliq).' Apply the rule that fa' imposes order among the suspended clauses.
The wife is non-consummated (ghayr al-mamsusa).
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Note that some earlier views treat fa' like waw, leading to three divorces. However, the correct (asahh) Hanafi position (agreed by all three imams) is that only one divorce occurs because fa' imposes order.
The first divorce immediately ends the marriage capacity, making subsequent divorces ineffective.
4
Justify the Hanafi position with the principle of order
Fa' requires that the suspended matters be arranged sequentially. Since the first talaq is effective, the following talaqs are either not triggered or are invalid because the subject (the marriage) no longer exists.
This is unlike waw, which does not impose order and would trigger all three simultaneously.
5
Examine the exception: fa' borrowed for waw in debts
In phrases like 'He owes me a dirham (fa) a dirham,' fa' is used like waw to mean 'and' because concrete objects cannot be ordered. The correct opinion is that both are due together, with a minimal sense of order (obligation of one precedes the other).
This shows the flexibility of fa' in different contexts.

غايات للعلل مقدمة عليها في التعقل، وفيه شيء، فإن دخول الفاء عليها ليس لإفادة تراخي العلل عنها في العقل، بل لإفادة عليتها، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية : الأولى أن يقال الفاء كما أنها تستعمل للتعقيب تستعمل للتعليل (ومنه) أي مما فيه الفاء داخلة على العلل. نحو : (أد فأنت حر أي لأنك حر وانزل فأنت آمن أي لأنك آمن فيثبت به العتق والأمان في الحال) وهذا لأن المتفاهم في أمثالهما هو هذا المعنى وقرينة كمال الانقطاع أيضاً موجودة واختلف الطلقات المعطوفة بها معلقة نحو : إن دخلت الدار فطالق فطالق فطالق لغير الممسوسة (فقيل: كالواو فعلى الخلاف كما مر فعنده تقع واحدة، وعندهما ثلاثاً (والأصح الاتفاق) أئمتنا بین الثلاثة ؛ (على) وقوع (الواحدة) فإن الفاء توجب الترتيب في المعلق فيجب أن تنزل مرتبات متراخياً بعضها عن بعض بخلاف العطف بالواو، إذ لم يكن هناك ترتيب في المعلقات (ويستعار) الفاء (اللواو) لوجود العلاقة بينهما (في نحو : له علي درهم فدرهم، فيلزم اثنان معاً إذ لا ترتيب في الأعيان) فلا يصح معنى الفاء (وقيل) لا يلزم منه أن لا يصح معنى الفاء أصلاً بل يراد أن وجوبه أسبق من وجوبه وهذا القدر من الترتيب كافٍ لصحة الفاء .
Endpoints for causes introduced upon them in [؟] intellect, and there is something in it; indeed, the entry of fa' upon them is not to indicate delay of causes in the intellect, but to indicate their causality. The 'Raider of Divine Secrets' said: The first thing to be said is that fa', just as it is used for sequence, is used for causality. (And from it) i.e., from that in which fa' enters upon causes. For example: 'Pay, for you are free,' i.e., because you are free, and 'Descend, for you are secure,' i.e., because you are secure; so freedom and security are established immediately. Indeed, fa' necessitates order in the suspended matter, so they must be arranged as sequential, one after another, unlike conjunction with waw, since there is no order in suspended matters. (And fa' is borrowed for waw) due to the relationship between them (in phrases like: 'He owes me a dirham, then a dirham,' so both are binding together since there is no order in concrete objects); thus the meaning of fa' does not apply. (And it was said) that from this it does not follow that the meaning of fa' does not apply at all; rather, what is intended is that its obligation precedes its obligation, and this degree of order is sufficient for the validity of fa'.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the linguistic rule regarding the letter fa' (ف) in legal discourse. The author first establishes that fa' indicates causality (ta'lil), not merely sequence. This is proven by examples like 'Pay, for you are free' where the freedom is the cause, not a later event. The 'Raider of Divine Secrets' is cited to affirm that fa' has both sequential and causal uses. The passage then applies this to suspended talaq (conditional divorce). For a non-consummated wife, if the husband says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, divorced, divorced' with fa', the correct Hanafi view (agreed upon by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is that only one talaq occurs. This is because fa' imposes order among the suspended pronouncements, so each subsequent talaq is contingent on the one before; since the first talaq makes divorce occur, the second and third are either not triggered or become invalid due to the expiration of the subject matter. The passage also discusses when fa' is borrowed for waw, as in a debt of two dirhams stated as 'dirham fad dirham' where both are due together because in concrete objects there is no sequential order. The correct opinion is that such usage is valid with a minimal degree of order.

Key Terms
الفاء (al-fa'): A letter used for sequence (ta'qib) and causality (ta'lil); in legal contexts, it may impose order among suspended clauses.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): Indicating the reason or cause for the action.
غير الممسوسة (ghayr al-mamsusa): A wife who has not been touched (consummated) by her husband, i.e., a non-madhkhul biha.

A) One talaq
B) Two talaq
C) Three talaq
D) No talaq

Key Takeaway
Fa' in suspended talaq imposes order, so only one divorce is effective; this distinguishes it from waw which would make all divorces occur simultaneously.

Dispute over Thumma: Delay in Speech or Ruling?
Usul dispute with critical refinement of Abu Hanifa's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on thumma in suspended talaq, identify the Sahibayn's preferred view, and analyze the critiques of Abu Hanifa's position using usul principles.

Core Idea
Thumma delays the ruling, not the speech—the Sahibayn's view is the stronger position in Hanafi usul.

The particle 'thumma' (ثم) generally indicates delay (tarakhi). But what exactly does it delay? Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) famously disagreed on this when applied to suspended talaq. Their difference leads to concrete legal consequences in how divorce pronouncements take effect. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the arguments on each side, and the preferred view that 'thumma' delays the ruling itself, not the speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The dispute centers on what thumma delays: the speech (utterance) or the ruling (legal effect). Abu Hanifa says speech; the Sahibayn say ruling.
2
Apply to suspended talaq
Given a statement like 'If you enter, you are divorced thumma divorced thumma divorced', trace how each view treats the divorce pronouncements.
For a non-consummated wife, the capacity for divorce is limited.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa treats thumma as a pause in speech, so only the talaq immediately following the condition is suspended; the next is immediate and the third invalid (in the non-consummated case).
4
Examine the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn hold that all talaq are suspended by the condition; they occur upon fulfillment, limited only by the wife's capacity. Thumma delays the ruling, not the speech.
5
Critique and tarjih
The passage presents a detailed critique of Abu Hanifa's position, showing it leads to logical absurdities, and declares the Sahibayn's view 'ashbah' (more resembling).
The 'Raider of Divine Secrets' (Matali' al-Asrar) reinforces this tarjih.

مسألة (مسألة ثم للتراخي في الحكم مع مهلة (وجاء) ثم (البيان المنزلة) كما يقال : صلى الله على محمد، ثم أبي بكر ثم ثم أبي بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان ثم علي رضي الله عنهم وشاع في الانتقال من مطلب إلى مطلب قالوا : يقع الثلاث في الحال معاً في المدخول بها في قوله (أنت طالق ثم) طالق ( ثم) طالق ( لأن حكم الإنشاء لا يتأخر عنه فلو اعتبر ههنا التراخي والمهلة يلزم تخلف الحكم عن الإنشاء المنجز هذا خلف، فبطل المهلة واعتبر أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه التراخي في التكلم في كلمة ثم فكأنه تكلم بالمعطوف عليه أولاً ثم سكت ثم تكلم بما بعد ثم وهكذا إذا علق بالشرط مقدماً) كان المعلق (أو مؤخراً فلم يتعلق به أي بالشرط (حقيقة إلا الملاصق به) فإذا قال لغير المدخولة : إن دخلت فطالق ثم طالق ثم طالق، يتعلق الأول بالشرط ويقع الثاني حالاً ويلغو الثالث وفي تأخير الشرط يقع الأول حالاً ويلغو الأخيران وإن قال للمدخولة يقع

الأول والثاني ويتعلق الثالث في تأخير الشرط، ويتعلق الأول ويقع الثاني والثالث في تقديم الشرط، وهذا لأنه عنده كالسكوت وفيه لا يتعلق بالشرط إلا الملاصق، فكذا ههنا، إلا أن غير الممسوسة لا تصلح إلا لوقوع فإما أن يكون مفاد كلمة ثم وهو بديهي البطلان فإنه لا دلالة له إلا على التراخي إما أنه في التكلم فلا يفهم وإما أن يكون لازماً له لزوماً خارجياً، وهو أيضاً باطل، لأن الوصل موجود بالضرورة، وإما أن يكون لازماً ذهنياً عرفياً أو عقلياً، فذلك أيضاً ،باطل، فإنا نسمع بالألسنة كلمة «ثم ونفهم مدلوله، ولا يخطر بالبال التراخي في التكلم أصلاً، وإما أن يكون لازماً شرعياً جعل الشارع هذا الوصل كلا وصل، ورتب عليه أحكام التراخي فلا بد من إبانته بدليل صاف عن غوائل الشبهات هذا ووجه بعضهم قول الإمام بأنه إنما أهدر الاتصال التكلمي قولاً بكمال التراخي. وهذا غير وافٍ فإن هذا النحو من الكمال أي جعل الموجود الثابت هدراً لا يساعده العرف في كلمة «ثم» ووجه صدر الشريعة بأنه إنما قال ذلك لئلا يتراخى حكم الإنشاء عنه، والأصل عدم التراخي، وهذا أيضاً غير واف، لأن كلمة «ثم» مانعة عن الوصل في الحكم كما يكون الشرط مانعاً، وحاكم بعضهم بأنه على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة هذا بإبداء المانع ، وأما على تقدير عدم جواز العلة فلا بد من هذا القول أي التراخي في التكلم لأنه لو تراخى الحكم فقط عن تخصيص التكلم به لزم تخصيص العلة وهو عند تخلف الحكم، لمانع أن العلة منتفية لأنه مع عدم المانع علة فكذا ههنا الإنشاء فقط ليس علة، بل هو مع عدم المانع، وههنا كلمة ثم مانعة، ثم لي سؤال آخر أنه : لو سلم التراخي في التكلم ينبغي أن تقع الطلقات متراخية مع مهلة، وأنتم لا تقولون به، بل أبطلتم التراخي والمهلة سابقاً فيما نجز فيه لئلا يلزم التراخي عن السبب، فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار التراخي في التكلم فإنه لا يلزم تراخي حكم الإنشاء عنه مع بقاء الوصل في Issue: (Issue: thumma for delay in the ruling with a respite. And thumma came (for explaining the status) as it is said: May Allah bless Muhammad, then Abu Bakr, then Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then 'Uthman, then 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, and it is common for moving from one topic to another. They said: The three occur together immediately for the consummated wife in his saying 'You are divorced, thumma divorced, thumma divorced' because the ruling of the construction (insha) is not delayed from it; if delay and respite were considered here, it would necessitate the ruling being delayed from the immediate construction, which is a contradiction. So respite is nullified. And Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, considered delay in speech in the word thumma, as if he spoke the conjoined first, then paused, then spoke what follows thumma, and so on. If it is suspended by a condition, whether the condition is advanced or delayed, nothing is actually suspended by the condition except the immediately adjacent one. So if he says to a non-consummated wife: 'If you enter, (you are) divorced, thumma divorced, thumma divorced', the first is suspended on the condition, the second occurs immediately, and the third is invalid. And in delaying the condition, the first occurs immediately, and the last two are invalid. And if he says to a consummated wife, [the first and second occur and the third is suspended in delayed condition; the first is suspended and the second and third occur in advanced condition]. (And the two companions suspended them all by the condition) i.e., for both consummated and non-consummated (so they occur upon the existence of the condition) in non-consummated one due to order in occurrence, and with the first the capacity is lost; and in consummated (all occur ordered) due to the capacity of the subject for them. The author said: (And it (i.e., their saying) is the more resembling (ashbah). And the 'Raider of Divine Secrets' reinforced it in 'Sharh al-Manar' that if delay in speech is [claimed], then it is either the very meaning of thumma (which is obviously false, as thumma has no indication of delay in speech), or an external necessary consequence (also false, because connection in speech is necessarily present), or a customary/intellectual necessary consequence (also false: we hear the word thumma and understand its meaning without any thought of delay in speech), or a legal necessary consequence (where the Lawgiver treats this connected speech as disconnected and attaches legal rulings of delay, requiring a clear proof free from doubts). Some explained the Imam's statement as merely discarding speech-connection to achieve complete delay, but this is insufficient because such discarding is not supported by custom in the word thumma. Sadr al-Shari'ah explained that he said so to avoid delaying the ruling of the insha, and the default is no delay; this is also insufficient because the word thumma prevents connection in the ruling just as a condition prevents. Some ruled that on the assumption that specifying the cause (takhsis al-illa) is permissible by presenting a preventer (mani'), it is acceptable; otherwise, this statement (delay in speech) is necessary because if only the ruling were delayed without specifying the speech, it would entail specifying the cause (which is speech). The 'Raider of Divine Secrets' said that even if we concede the invalidity of specifying the cause, it is not complete: we do not accept that the insha is the cause for the existence of the ruling in actuality, but rather according to its requirement. 'You are divorced' means 'divorced immediately', making it a cause for immediate divorce. If thumma is added, it becomes a cause for delayed occurrence. Thus we say what the opponents of specifying the cause say: the cause is absent due to a preventer. Furthermore, even if we accept delay in speech, the talaqs should occur with delay and respite, yet you (Abu Hanifa) do not say that; you previously nullified delay and respite in immediate (non-suspended) cases to avoid delay from the cause. So what is the need to consider delay in speech? It does not necessitate delay of the ruling from the insha while speech-connection remains. So considering delay in speech after declaring the invalidity of delay [in ruling] is inconsistent.
It is completed.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute regarding the meaning of thumma (ثم) in legal constructions, specifically its effect on suspended talaq. Thumma generally indicates delay (tarakhi) with a respite. The passage begins by stating the common usage of thumma for transition. For an immediate (unconditional) talaq with thumma, such as 'You are divorced, thumma divorced, thumma divorced' from a consummated wife, the ruling is that all three occur at once because the insha (enunciation) cannot be delayed after its utterance. Abu Hanifa, however, considered that thumma implies a delay in the speech itself (tarakhi fi al-takallum), as if the speaker pauses. This leads to specific rules for suspended talaq: only the talaq immediately adjacent to the condition is suspended; others either occur at once or are invalid. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that all talaq are suspended by the condition, so they occur together when the condition is fulfilled. For a non-consummated wife, only one occurs due to her limited capacity; for a consummated wife, all three occur in order. The author declares the companions' view as 'ashbah' (more resembling). The rest of the passage is a critical analysis defending this preference, refuting the notion of delay in speech through multiple arguments, and showing inconsistencies in Abu Hanifa's position. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon view in the madhhab is that thumma does not cause a delay in speech; rather, it delays the ruling, and all suspended talaq operate together under the condition.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A letter indicating delay (tarakhi) with a respite, used for transition or ordering.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): The legal principle of delay or postponement.
المدخولة (al-madkhuula): A wife who has been consummated (touched).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred (ashbah) view, what happens when a non-consummated wife is told 'If you enter, you are divorced (thumma) divorced (thumma) divorced'?
A) All three are suspended; one occurs when condition is met
B) First is suspended; second occurs immediately; third is invalid
C) All three occur immediately upon speaking
D) None are valid

Key Takeaway
Thumma delays the ruling, not the speech; therefore, in suspended talaq, all pronouncements are suspended and occur together upon fulfillment of the condition, limited only by the wife's capacity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
The Dispute over 'ثم' in Conditional Divorce: Delay in Speech or Ruling?
Dispute on linguistic particle in usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of the particle 'ثم' (thumma) in conditional legal statements and evaluate the Hanafi preference for the Sahibayn's view over Imam Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
The particle 'ثم' indicates delay in the ruling, not just speech — the Sahibayn's view is preferred.

In this lesson, we examine a classic dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: does the word 'ثم' (then) in a conditional divorce indicate a delay in the speech or a delay in the legal effect? The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued for delay in the ruling, while Imam Abu Hanifa held that only speech is delayed. Through a detailed analysis, the text concludes that the companions' view is more appropriate (ashbah). This dispute illustrates how linguistic particles are interpreted in legal contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the view of Imam Abu Hanifa (tarākhī fī al-takallum — delay in speech) and the view of the two companions (tarākhī fī al-ḥukm — delay in the legal ruling).
The core disagreement is whether 'ثم' delays the utterance or the legal effect.
2
Trace the key arguments for each
For Abu Hanifa: the construct (insha') is a cause for immediate effect, and the original state is no delay. For the companions: the linguistic meaning of 'ثم' indicates order and delay, which should apply to the ruling.
Abu Hanifa's argument relies on the principle that the legal effect attaches immediately to the utterance.
3
Analyze the refutations presented
The text refutes attempts to justify Abu Hanifa's view: custom does not support delaying speech, and the problem of a limit for the mufti is common to both views.
The refutation shows that 'ثم' does not customarily imply a pause in speech.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
In an untouched wife, Abu Hanifa rules two divorces (both utterances take effect immediately), while the companions rule one divorce (the second is delayed and the place is lost).
This practical difference shows the real impact of the usul dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text declares the companions' view as 'ashbah' (more similar to the truth) based on linguistic custom and consistency.
The tarjih is supported by detailed rational arguments from Sharh al-Manar and Miftah al-Asrar.

والأصل عدم التراخي، وهذا أيضاً غير واف، لأن كلمة «ثم» مانعة عن الوصل في الحكم كما يكون الشرط مانعاً، وحاكم بعضهم بأنه على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة هذا بإبداء المانع ، وأما على تقدير عدم جواز العلة فلا بد من هذا القول أي التراخي في التكلم لأنه لو تراخى الحكم فقط عن تخصيص التكلم به لزم تخصيص العلة وهو التكلم ، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية رحمه الله في بعض كتبه إنه إن سلم بطلان تخصيص العلة فلا يتم أيضاً، فإنا لا نسلم أن الإنشاء علة لوجود الحكم بالفعل بل على حسب اقتضائه فأنت طالق إذ معناه طالق في الحال، صار سبباً لوقوع الطلاق في الحال، وإذا زيد عند الدخول صار علة للوقوع عنده فيجوز أن يكون إذا زيد كلمة ثم يكون سبباً للوقوع متراخياً عن الأول، على أنا نقول فيه مثل ما يقول مانعو التخصيص في العلة عند تخلف الحكم، لمانع أن العلة منتفية لأنه مع عدم المانع علة فكذا ههنا الإنشاء فقط ليس علة، بل هو مع عدم المانع، وههنا كلمة ثم مانعة، ثم لي سؤال آخر أنه : لو سلم التراخي في التكلم ينبغي أن تقع الطلقات متراخية مع مهلة، وأنتم لا تقولون به، بل أبطلتم التراخي والمهلة سابقاً فيما نجز فيه لئلا يلزم التراخي عن السبب، فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار التراخي في التكلم فإنه لا يلزم تراخي حكم الإنشاء عنه مع بقاء الوصل في التكلم وحينئذٍ فاعتبار التراخي في التكلم لئلا يلزم التراخي في الإنشاء له بعد القول ببطلان التراخي لذلك غير معقول ولا يستطيع هذا العبد أن يتصوره، فضلاً عن التصديق به، هذا ولم لا يجوز أن يبطل التراخي بأصله؟ وقيل في توجيه تقوية كلام الإمام أن اعتبار التراخي مشكل للمفتي في الحكم، فإنه لا حد له بخلاف التراخي في التكلم فإنه يمكن اعتباره بقدر ما يمنع الاستثناء وغيره، وهذا أيضاً غير واف فإنه مشترك بينهما إذ يجوز أن يعتبر في الحكم أيضاً أقل ما يعد في العرف تراخياً، ثم إنه قد تقدم أنه تسقط المهلة في الإنشاءات فلا تعسر على المفتي أصلاً هذا
And they (the two companions) attached (the divorce) to the condition in both cases (the touched and untouched wife), so it occurs upon the existence of the condition. In the non-intercourse case, one divorce occurs due to the order (tartīb) of occurrence, and with the first the place is lost. And in her case (the touched wife), all (divorces) occur, arranged, because the place is suitable for them. The author said: 'And it (the saying of the two companions) is more similar (ashbah).' And 'Mutla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah' in 'Sharh al-Manar' supported it by stating that if delay in speech is considered, then either it is the meaning of the word 'thumma' — which is obviously false, as it only indicates delay in meaning, not in speech — or it is an external necessary concomitant, which is also false because connection necessarily exists, or it is a customary or rational necessary concomitant, which is also false, as we hear the word 'thumma' and understand its meaning without any idea of delay in speech. Or it is a legal necessary concomitant, making the connection as if non-existent, but this requires a clear proof. Some explained Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement as disregarding the speech connection to achieve complete delay. But this is insufficient, as such complete disregard is not supported by custom in the word 'thumma'. Sadr al-Shari'ah explained that he said that so that the ruling of the construct (insha') is not delayed, and the principle is no delay. This is also insufficient, because 'thumma' prevents connection in the ruling just as a condition prevents. Some ruled that if specification of the cause (takhsis al-'illa) is permissible, this is with a preventative; if not, then the statement of delay in speech is necessary. Then 'Mutla' al-Asrar' argued that even if invalidity of specification of the cause is granted, it still fails, because we do not accept that the construct is a cause for the existence of the ruling actually, but according to its requirement. 'You are divorced' means 'divorced now', becoming a cause for immediate divorce. When 'at the entry' is added, it becomes a cause for occurrence at that time. So when 'thumma' is added, it can be a cause for occurrence delayed from the first. We say about it like those who prevent specification say when the ruling is absent: due to a preventative, the cause is absent. Here, the construct alone is not the cause, but it is with the absence of a preventative. Here 'thumma' is a preventative. Then I have another question: if delay in speech is granted, then the divorces should occur with a delay and respite, but you do not say that; you previously invalidated delay and respite in immediate constructs to avoid delay from the cause. So what need is there to consider delay in speech? Since it does not require delay in the ruling of the construct while preserving the connection in speech. And then considering delay in speech to avoid delay in the construction after claiming invalidation of delay is incomprehensible. This (consideration) is not rational, and this servant cannot conceive it, let alone believe it. Why is it not permissible to invalidate delay? It was said in support of the Imam's statement that considering delay is problematic for the mufti in the ruling, as it has no limit, unlike delay in speech which can be considered to the extent of preventing exceptions etc. But this is also insufficient, as it is common to both, since one could consider in the ruling also the least that is considered delay in custom. Moreover, it has been stated that respite is dropped in constructs, so there is no difficulty for the mufti at all. This.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the effect of the word 'ثم' (then) in a conditional divorce. The author begins by stating the position of the two companions: that when the condition is attached with 'ثم', the divorce occurs at the time of the condition, but with a specific ordering. In the case of an untouched wife, only one divorce occurs because the place (mahall) is lost after the first. In the case of a touched wife, all divorces occur in order because the place is suitable. The author then reports that the preferred view (الأشبه) is that of the two companions. The commentary then launches into an elaborate argumentation supporting this preference, drawing from 'Sharh al-Manar' and 'Miftaḥ al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah'. The key issue is whether the word 'ثم' indicates a delay in the speech (al-tarākhī fī al-takallum) or a delay in the legal ruling (al-tarākhī fī al-ḥukm). Abu Hanifa held that 'ثم' indicates a delay in speech, meaning that the second condition is uttered after a pause, but the legal effect is immediate. The companions held that 'ثم' indicates a delay in the legal effect. The commentary refutes various attempts to justify Abu Hanifa's position, arguing that the customary understanding of 'ثم' does not support delay in speech, and that the need for a mufti to have a limit for delay does not necessitate delay in speech. The final conclusion supports the companions' view. This is a usul dispute about the interpretation of a linguistic particle in legal contexts.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle of conjunction indicating order and delay (tarākhī). In this dispute, whether the delay is in speech or in the ruling.
التراخي في التكلم (al-tarākhī fī al-takallum): The view that the word 'ثم' indicates that the second statement is uttered after a pause, but the legal effect of both statements is immediate.
التراخي في الحكم (al-tarākhī fī al-ḥukm): The view that 'ثم' indicates that the legal effect of the second statement occurs after a delay from the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (الأشبه) in this passage, in the dispute about the word 'ثم' in conditional divorce, which position is considered more correct?
A) The view of Imam Abu Hanifa
B) The view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
C) The view of Imam Shafi'i
D) The view of Imam Zufar

Key Takeaway
The particle 'ثم' in conditional divorce indicates a delay in the legal effect, not just a pause in speech, according to the preferred Hanafi view.

The Effect of 'Bal' in Iqrar: Linguistic Analysis and the Hanafi Position
Analyzing the effect of 'bal' in iqrar with a refutation of Zufar's qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effect of the particle 'bal' in iqrar (admission) according to Hanafi usul, evaluate Zufar's opposing view, and apply the principle that iqrar is khabar not insha'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'bal' in iqrar diverts from singularity to multiplicity, not nullifying the first admission.

This passage tackles a nuanced usul dispute: if a person says 'dirham bal dirhaman', how many dirhams does he owe? Imam Zufar argued for three, analogizing to divorce declarations. The Hanafi majority holds that only two are owed, because iqrar is a report (khabar) that can be refined without retraction. Let us unpack the linguistic and usul reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
Classify the speech act
Determine whether iqrar is insha' (performative) or khabar (informative). This sets the epistemological framework.
Hanafi usul treats iqrar as khabar, unlike divorce which is insha'.
2
Interpret the particle 'bal'
Analyze its function in singular noun contexts: is it for ibtal (nullification) or idrab (turning away from a quality)?
In singular nouns, 'bal' typically diverts from the quality of singularity.
3
Apply the rule to the iqrar
Show that the first admission remains intact; 'bal' adds another dirham, so total is two.
The first admission is not retracted; it serves as foundation for the increase.
4
Refute the qiyas on insha'
Explain why the analogy to divorce fails: iqrar does not immediately fix a third-party right.
In insha', the ruling takes effect instantly and cannot be undone; in khabar, the speaker can correct himself.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this make? Two dirhams vs. three dirhams.
The disagreement has a direct financial consequence.

يقتضيه هذا الكلام الآخر فلزم موجبهما وبطل الإعراض بهذا الوجه شرعاً، لا أنه لا تصح الإرادة من الكلام لغة هذا والله أعلم بأحكامه .
Subsidiary issue: Imam Zufar said that three become obligatory when he says 'I owe a dirham, bal two dirhams,' but (not because bal two dirhams is a nullification of the first, for he cannot nullify the iqrar, so the second with the first becomes necessary, thus three dirhams become necessary (as has been said). But this is not correct, because bal in the singular is not for nullification; rather, because the turning away from the iqrar is a retraction and an invalid withdrawal. Here the declarant intends to use the word bal and make the iqrar of a dirham like something unmentioned, and this is not within his capacity, so the iqrar of two dirhams with the first becomes necessary, thus three become necessary. And this is not like istithna' (exception), because when he says 'I owe three except one,' two become necessary, because he spoke of the remainder after the exception, so it is as if he only spoke of iqrar of two. And this (i.e., bal dirhaman) is idrab after speech. We say: it is admitted that it is idrab, but what is customary in nouns of number is that the idrab is regarding the quality of singularity. So what is established is not an individual dirham but two dirhams, so he makes iqrar of the extra, and in the extra there is admission of the increased amount, so the iqrar is not nullified by this idrab, thus it is valid. And it might be objected here that idrab regarding singularity is a branch of understanding multiplicity, and then one must adopt the concept of number (mafhum al-'adad), and we have been forbidden from it. The answer is that singularity can be in that the other is unmentioned, and it is not necessary from singularity to judge the absence of the other, so understanding singularity does not necessitate understanding the concept. So in the example given, he makes idrab from the singularity of the dirham in the iqrar, and makes with it another as mentioned and admitted. And it is also answered that what we are forbidden from is understanding the concept through context, and here idrab is a context for understanding the concept, so consider. And his qiyas (analogy) meaning Zufar's analogy upon insha' such as 'you are divorced once, bal twice,' where three occur, is invalid because of a difference. Because iqrar is khabar (informative) according to the soundest view, so it does not establish anything, so no branching upon the wording for ruling. So he can turn away from a report, as if he reported it and then reports another report in its place, unlike insha' because ruling is established by it, and after its establishment it is not in his hand to turn away from it. And one may say that insha' and iqrar are equal: because either the idrab in iqrar is about mere singularity, meaning he does not have one with the quality of singularity but rather with another, so too in insha' it is permissible that the turning away is from the quality of singularity, meaning it is not a divorce with a single divorce only but with another one, so she is divorced twice. Or the idrab is about the iqrar of the dirham itself, then the turning away should not be valid because it is a retraction, and that is not to be heard, especially since it pertains to the right of another, just as retraction in insha' is not allowed because it is not in his hand. So there is no difference between them. The answer, with success from Allah, is that it is a turning away from the single with the quality of unity, and establishing it with another via another report, namely bal two. This is within his capability, because retraction in iqrar is only invalid because it involves the right of another, and by retraction the right of another would be invalidated, but retraction with the word bal does not invalidate the right at all, rather it affirms it, because he only retracts to show the increase. This is unlike insha', because once he has uttered a single divorce, it occurred with the quality of unity, because in insha' the ruling is not delayed, and he made himself the cause of the ruling, so it is not in his ability to nullify it at all, nor to nullify it with this quality and establish it with another speech with another quality, because what has occurred cannot be removed. So if he intends by that to turn away from the first and effect a new insha' with another speech, it does not nullify what he turned away from because its cause exists, and what this other speech necessitates occurs, so both become necessary and the turning away in this respect is void according to Sharia, not that the intention from the speech is invalid linguistically. This, and Allah knows best His rulings.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of a subsidiary issue (far') concerning the effect of the word 'bal' in a declaration (iqrar). Imam Zufar held that if someone says 'I owe a dirham, bal two dirhams,' he must pay three dirhams, because 'bal' nullifies the first iqrar and adds the second, so both are owed. The author rejects this, arguing that 'bal' in the singular does not nullify, but rather diverts from the quality of singularity to multiplicity. The declarant is not retracting the first iqrar; he is clarifying that the debt is not one individual dirham but two, so only two are owed. The author compares this to istithna' (exception), where the exclusion is part of the same speech. He also refutes Zufar's analogy to insha' (performative utterances) like divorce. In iqrar (a report), the speaker can change his report because no one's right has been fixed yet; in insha' (divorce), the ruling takes effect immediately and cannot be undone. Even though the declarant may intend to divert from the first, the first iqrar remains valid as a foundation for admitting the increase. The passage ultimately affirms the Hanafi position that 'bal' in iqrar confirms the first and adds the second, so only two dirhams are owed.

Key Terms
إضراب (idrab): Turning away or diverting from one meaning to another, typically with the particle 'bal'.
إقرار (iqrar): A declaration or admission, treated as khabar (informative statement) in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One dirham
B) Two dirhams
C) Three dirhams
D) Nothing, because the iqrar is contradictory

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'bal' in an iqrar serves to divert from the quality of singularity, not to nullify the first admission; thus the total is the sum of both parts.

The Particle 'Bal' in Conditional Divorce
Analysing the effect of 'bal' on suspended divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule for the particle 'bal' to determine the number of divorces in suspended divorce statements and distinguish it from conjunction with 'waw'.

Core Idea
With 'bal', only the second part counts—the first is nullified, making the speech a single unit.

This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi usul principle concerning the particle 'bal' (but rather) in conditional divorce. Unlike 'waw' which adds independent clauses, 'bal' indicates a turning away from the first statement, making the entire expression depend on the second part. Through linguistic analysis and analogy, the Hanafi school derives a clear ruling that only the part after 'bal' has legal effect. Understanding this principle sharpens your ability to interpret suspended utterances in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conjunction
Determine whether 'bal' or another particle (like 'waw') is used in the conditional statement.
The legal outcome hinges on this distinction.
2
Recognize the modifying effect of 'bal'
Understand that 'bal' is a modifier (مغير) that changes the prior ruling, not merely adds to it.
This is the key difference from 'waw'.
3
Apply the dependency rule
The beginning of speech depends on its end when a modifier like 'bal' is present; the speech is considered one unit.
This is derived from the general usul principle.
4
Consider the analogy from declarative sentences
Analogize from Ibn al-Humam's example: 'No man came but two men' where the first part is nullified and only the second is operative.
This qiyas shows the same logic applies in conditional divorce.
5
Derive the ruling
Conclude that only what follows 'bal' takes effect, whether the divorce is immediate or suspended.
The first number is a mere prelude and has no legal effect.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

That: it has preceded that this is different from conjunction with waw) as when he says: 'If you enter, you are divorced one and two' then according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] one divorce occurs, because in conjunction with waw the conjunct is linked by means of the conjoined, so its attachment is after the attachment of the first as previously mentioned, and it does not stand in place of the first (so reflect). Then I have here a discussion: the beginning of speech depends on its end if there is a modifier like exception, condition and the like, and the first is considered with the last as one speech, so the entire speech is acted upon. There is no doubt that the word 'bal' modifies the ruling before it, so the beginning of speech depends on its end. Also it is not independent, so it needs a speech to which it is linked, thus it depends on it. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam stated that in examples like 'No man came but two men' and 'No men in the house but two men', his words 'but two men' are a specifier, and the specified depends on the specifier, otherwise contradiction would occur in informing of something then turning to another report like 'my age is seventy but ninety'. When it is established that the first depends on the last in conjunction with 'bal', then his saying 'you are divorced one' does not benefit until 'but two' is added to it. Likewise, it does not attach to his saying 'if you enter' unless 'but two' is added to it, then his abandonment of the one and effecting the two instead is valid, whether immediate as in the first branch or suspended as in the second, for he may retract what he has not effected nor suspended. Rather we say: effecting the two and suspending them have two expressions, longer and shorter. He may express with a longer expression by mentioning something first then turning away from it and mentioning the intended, then attributing the ruling to it with increased concern for its importance. This is the modification with 'bal'. So there is no attribution to the first, rather it is brought only to turn away from it to the attributed. So nothing occurs nor is suspended except what is after 'bal'. Understand this. This is what I have, and perhaps Allah will bring about something after that.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage explains the usul rule regarding the particle 'bal' (بل) when used in conditional divorce. The author distinguishes 'bal' from 'waw' ('and'). In 'waw' conjunction, each term is independent, so both clauses take effect. But 'bal' indicates a turning away from the first to the second, making the first dependent on the second. Therefore, when a husband says, 'If you enter, you are divorced one, but (بل) two', only the second number ('two') counts, because 'bal' nullifies the first and substitutes the second. This is supported by Ibn al-Humam's analogy with declarative sentences: 'No man came but two men' means 'two men came', and the first part ('no man') is not operative independently. The ruling is that the first clause is merely a prelude that does not produce legal effect until the second clause, which contains the intended ruling, is attached. This is a purely Hanafi position, as other schools may treat 'bal' differently in such contexts.

Key Terms
بل (bal): A particle of turning away (الإضراب) that nullifies the first part and makes the second the intended ruling.
المخصص (al-mukhassis): The specifier that determines the intended meaning after an initial vague statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce occurs.
B) Two divorces occur.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) One divorce occurs only if he intends it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the particle 'bal' in conditional divorce nullifies the first number, making only the second number legally effective.

The Particle 'Ala: Definitions and Legal Uses
Definition and classification of the particle 'ala' in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main legal uses of the particle 'ala' in Hanafi usul and distinguish between its literal and figurative applications.

Core Idea
'Ala can mean elevation, exchange attachment, or condition depending on legal context.

The particle 'ala' is a small word with significant legal consequences. In Hanafi usul, it is used in three distinct senses: literal elevation (e.g., debt), attachment in commutative contracts (sale, marriage, lease), and condition in divorce according to Abu Hanifa. Understanding these uses is essential for correct ruling derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of 'ala
Examine the sentence where 'ala appears. Is it in a debt acknowledgment, a contract, or a divorce pronouncement?
The same preposition shifts meaning based on the legal field.
2
Classify the use as literal or figurative
For debt, 'ala is literal (elevation of obligation). For contracts, it is figuratively used for attachment (ilsaq). For divorce, it is disputed: condition or compensation.
The literal meaning is 'elevation' (isti'la'), extended metaphorically.
3
Apply the appropriate Hanafi usul principle
The principle: al-haqiqah tukhrij 'an al-majaz (literal meaning is default). Where a contextual indicator (qarinah) exists, majaz is applied.
For contracts, the qarinah of exchange is present, so 'ala is majaz for ilsaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة على للاستعلاء ولو معنى أي ولو كان الاستعلاء معنوياً فيعم اللزوم، كالدين) فإن فيه استعلاء معنى يقال ركبه الدين واستعير في المعاوضات المحضة أي العقود التي لا تنعقد إلا بمعاوضة المال (كالنكاح والإجارة والبيع للإلصاق) بمعنى باء المقابلة بالاتفاق كاحمله على عشرة، أو بعتك هذا العبد على عشرة، أو تزوجت على عشرة (و) استعير (في الطلاق للشرط) أي لكون ما بعده معلقاً بما قبله عنده، ففي طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف، لا شيء له بواحدة) أي لا شيء للزوج بإيقاع واحدة لعدم انقسام المشروط على الشرط) فإن حاصل التعليق أن المشروط ثابت على تقدير تحقق الشرط، وأما أن كل بعض منه ثابت على تقدير كل بعض من الشرط فلا فلو ثبت ثبت من غير مقتض فلا يثبت، ولعل هذا مراد من قال إنه انقسم انقسام أجزاء المشروط قبل الشرط وإلا فيرد وروداً ظاهراً أنه كما وجد بعض المشروط وجد بعض الشرط، فعلى تقدير انقسام أجزاء المشروط على أجزاء الشرط يكون كل جزء من المشروط مشروطاً بجزء من الشرط فلا استحالة وأيضاً لا استحالة في تقدم جزء المشروط على الشرط إنما المحال تقدم نفس المشروط على الشرط (وعندهما) يستعار في الطلاق (للإلصاق عوضاً، فينقسم) أجزاء العوض على أجزاء المعوض (فله (الثلث للألف في طلاق واحد (أقول ترجيحهما كما في «التحرير» بأن الأصل فيما علمت مقابلته بمال العوضية) والطلاق مما يقابل بمال، فيحمل فيه على العوضية ضعيف لأن ذلك أي كون العوضية أصلاً (فيما لا يحتمل الشرط المحض أصلاً كالبيع ونحوه، لا في كل ما يقبل المعاوضة في الجملة، هذا وقد يدفع بدعوى الاستقراء والله أعلم ( كترجيحه) أي كما أن ترجيح قول الإمام ضعيف (بأنه) أي على (مجاز في الإلصاق حقيقة في الشرط فيحمل عليه عند إمكانه ( كما ذكره شمس الأئمة) وإنما كان ضعيفاً (لأنه) أي كونه حقيقة في الشرط ممنوع قيل في الاستناد (لأن الإلصاق) المتحقق في العوض حقيقته أي حقيقة على فإنه من أفراد اللزوم) إذ هناك يلزم العوض في الذمة (أقول : اللزوم إنما يتحقق بعد التعلق) الذي يكون في المعاوضة (لأنه يوجب المقابلة، والمقابلة توجب اللزوم فالتعلق يوجب اللزوم والكلام في أصل التعلق) إنه حقيقة فيه أم لا (بعد) فالحق أن الإلصاق والشرطية كلاهما غير اللزوم، فهو فيهما ،مجاز، هذا ومن ادعى أنه حقيقة في الشرط لم يقل بأنه باعتبار اللغة حقيقة، بل يقول : صار في العرف حقيقة، بمعنى لا يحتاج في الانفهام إلى قرينة أصلاً، وهو غير ظاهر الفساد، لكن يلزم عليه البيان (ثم أقول لك أن ترجحه أي قول الإمام بأن تعلق المجموع من الألف (بالمجموع) من الطلقات صوناً عن الإلغاء ضروري سواء كان التعلق شرطياً أو إلصاقياً (وانقسام البعض على البعض زائد بلا دليل فإنه إن كان للشرط فظاهر أنه لا انقسام وإن كان للإلصاق (فإن الطلاق يحتمل الأمرين بعوض المال وبغير عوض المال ولا قيمة له في ذاته أصلاً، حتى يقسم عليها إلا بالشرط والرضا، وقد وقع بتقويم المجموع لا الأجزاء بخلاف البيع ونحوه) فإن للعوضين قيمة في ذاتيهما، فلا بد أن تقع في مقابلة الأجزاء التي هي أموال أجزاء من العوض الآخر وإلاّ لزم بقاء المال بلا عوض، وإذا كان مقابلة الأجزاء بالأجزاء بلا دليل فلم يثبت) . (فرع . في قول رجل له علي ألف يلزم (الدين ويكون إقراراً به لكونه حقيقة في اللزوم وهو كونه ديناً ولو) وصل وديعة تعين (المجاز لوجود الصارف (وهو وجوب الحفظ). ليس ممتداً
Issue: 'ala is for elevation even if metaphorical, i.e., even if the elevation is metaphorical, it generalizes obligation, like debt. It is borrowed in pure commutative contracts, i.e., contracts that are only concluded with exchange of property, like marriage, lease, and sale, for attachment, meaning the preposition 'ba' al-muqabala' by agreement, as in 'carry it for ten', or 'I sold you this slave for ten', or 'I married for ten'. And it is borrowed in divorce for condition, i.e., that what follows is suspended upon what precedes, in his (Abu Hanifa's) view. So in 'divorce me three times for a thousand', he gets nothing for one divorce, i.e., the husband gets nothing for effecting one divorce due to non-division of the conditioned upon the condition. The summary of suspension is that the conditioned is established upon the condition of realization of the condition. But that every part of it is established upon every part of the condition does not follow. If it were established, it would be without cause, so it is not established. Perhaps this is the intent of the one who said that it is divided into parts of the conditioned before the condition; otherwise, it is refuted obviously that as some conditioned exists, some condition exists. So on the assumption of division of parts of the conditioned upon parts of the condition, each part of the conditioned is conditioned by a part of the condition, so there is no impossibility. Also, there is no impossibility in the precedence of part of the conditioned over the condition; the impossible is the precedence of the conditioned itself over the condition. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is borrowed in divorce for attachment as compensation, so it divides parts of the compensation upon parts of the compensated. So he gets a third of the thousand for one divorce. I say: their preference, as in al-Tahrir, that the principle in what is known to be counterbalanced by property is compensation, and divorce is among that which is counterbalanced by property, so it is construed as compensation, is weak because that, i.e., compensation being the principle, is in what does not admit pure condition at all, like sale and similar, not in everything that admits exchange in general. This may be rebutted by claiming induction, and Allah knows best. Like his preference, i.e., that the preference of the Imam's statement is weak, because 'ala is metaphorical in attachment and literal in condition, so it is construed accordingly when possible, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma. It is weak because its being literal in condition is disputed; it was said in support because the attachment realized in compensation is its reality, i.e., the reality of 'ala, for it is a type of obligation, as the compensation is obligated in the liability. I say: obligation is realized only after attachment, which is in exchange, because it necessitates correspondence, and correspondence necessitates obligation. So attachment necessitates obligation, but the discussion is about the origin of attachment: whether it is literal in it or not. After all, the truth is that attachment and conditionality are both other than obligation, so it is metaphorical in both. One who claims it is literal in condition does not say it is literal in language, but says it became literal in custom, meaning it does not need a context to be understood, and this is not obviously corrupt, but it imposes clarification. Then I say you can prefer his, i.e., the Imam's statement, by saying that the attachment of the total of the thousand to the total of the divorces is necessary to avoid nullity, whether the attachment is conditional or compensational. And the division of some upon some is extraneous without evidence. If it is for condition, it is clear there is no division; if it is for attachment, then divorce admits both possibilities: with and without monetary compensation, and it has no value in itself to be divided upon except by condition and consent. It occurs by valuation of the total, not parts, unlike sale and similar, because the two considerations have value in themselves, so they must occur in exchange of parts that are property for parts of the other consideration; otherwise, property would remain without compensation. And if the matching of parts with parts is without evidence, it is not established. (Branch: In a man's saying 'I owe a thousand', the debt is established and it is an acknowledgment because 'ala is literal in obligation, i.e., it being a debt. If he added 'deposit', the figurative meaning is determined due to the presence of the indicator, i.e., the duty of preservation.) It is not extended.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the particle 'ala'. The discussion centers on its meanings in Islamic law. The text explains that 'ala can be used for physical or figurative elevation. In contracts like sale, lease, and marriage, it is used for attachment (ilsaq) similar to the preposition 'ba' for exchange. In divorce, the Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa views it as a condition (shart), meaning the divorce is conditional upon payment, so if only one divorce occurs, the husband gets nothing because the condition (three divorces) is not fulfilled. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) view it as attachment for compensation, meaning it divides the payment proportionally. The author critiques both preferences, siding with Abu Hanifa's reasoning that attaching the total sum to the total divorces avoids nullity, and division of parts is unsupported. The branch (far') applies 'ala's literal meaning of obligation to acknowledgment of debt.

Key Terms
على ('ala): Preposition indicating elevation (isti'la'), attachment (ilsaq) in contracts, or condition (shart) in divorce according to Abu Hanifa.
الإلصاق (al-ilsaq): Attachment; in contracts, 'ala means the exchange of one thing for another.
الشرط (al-shart): Condition; in divorce, 'ala makes the divorce dependent on payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'ala in the sale contract 'I sold you this slave for ten' (بعناك هذا العبد على عشرة)?
A) Physical elevation
B) Attachment for exchange (ilsaq)
C) Condition (shart)
D) Obligation (luzum)

Key Takeaway
The particle 'ala has multiple legal meanings: obligation in debt, exchange in contracts, and disputed condition/compensation in divorce.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Dispute on 'Ala in Divorce: Shart vs. Ilaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'ala in divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'ala in divorce and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: 'ala in divorce is condition (shart); Sahibayn: it is compensation (ilsaq ʻiwaḍ) — partial divorce yields nothing vs. proportional payment.

The small particle 'ala triggers a major dispute within the Hanafi school. When a husband says 'I divorce you three times for a thousand', does the payment depend on all three divorces (shart) or does it attach proportionally to each divorce (ilsaq)? This lesson unpacks the arguments and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions clearly
Abu Hanifa: 'ala indicates shart (condition), so the conditioned (full divorces) is suspended on the condition (full payment). Sahibayn: 'ala indicates ilsaq (attachment for compensation), so payment is divided proportionally.
The same phrase yields opposite outcomes.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
The total sum is attached to the total divorces. Division of the conditioned into parts would require evidence, which is absent. Also, the conditioned (divorce) cannot exist before the condition (payment).
Key concept: part of conditioned cannot precede part of condition.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
Divorce is a commutative contract (mu'awada) like sale, where compensation is the default. They analogize to sale: in sale, 'ala divides the price over the goods sold.
They argue the default of compensation applies because divorce can be financial.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The author argues that compensation default applies only where pure condition is impossible (like sale), not in all exchanges. Divorce can be both with and without payment, so condition is possible and thus preferred.
The response refutes the analogy.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If one divorce occurs: Abu Hanifa gives nothing; Sahibayn give one-third of the thousand.
This is the practical difference for fatwa.

Source Text

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Branch: Applying 'Ala to Debt Acknowledgment
Application of the literal meaning of 'ala in debt acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the literal meaning of 'ala to determine whether a statement constitutes an acknowledgment of debt and identify when a contextual indicator shifts its meaning.

Core Idea
When 'ala is used with a sum, it literally means obligation; adding 'deposit' forces a figurative reading.

This branch (far') illustrates how the usul rule about 'ala's literal meaning (obligation) operates in practice. When someone says 'I owe you a thousand' using 'ala, it is an acknowledgment of debt. But if they add 'deposit', the meaning changes because the context of deposit overrides the literal sense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the straightforward case
A man says: 'I have a thousand on you' (له علي ألف). Because 'ala literally means obligation here, it is an acknowledgment of debt.
This is the default ruling.
2
Identify the modifying context
If the man adds 'deposit' (وديعة), the literal meaning is overridden; it becomes a figurative claim about a deposit.
The indicator (qarinah) is 'deposit', which requires preservation, not payment.
3
Apply the usul rule of haqiqah and majaz
Literal meaning is default unless there is a contextual indicator (sarf). Here, 'deposit' is the indicator that shifts 'ala from obligation to figurative sense.
The phrase 'exists' (ممتد) is irrelevant; the passage ends with 'not extended', meaning the discussion is not continued.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة على للاستعلاء ولو معنى أي ولو كان الاستعلاء معنوياً فيعم اللزوم، كالدين) فإن فيه استعلاء معنى يقال ركبه الدين واستعير في المعاوضات المحضة أي العقود التي لا تنعقد إلا بمعاوضة المال (كالنكاح والإجارة والبيع للإلصاق) بمعنى باء المقابلة بالاتفاق كاحمله على عشرة، أو بعتك هذا العبد على عشرة، أو تزوجت على عشرة (و) استعير (في الطلاق للشرط) أي لكون ما بعده معلقاً بما قبله عنده، ففي طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف، لا شيء له بواحدة) أي لا شيء للزوج بإيقاع واحدة لعدم انقسام المشروط على الشرط) فإن حاصل التعليق أن المشروط ثابت على تقدير تحقق الشرط، وأما أن كل بعض منه ثابت على تقدير كل بعض من الشرط فلا فلو الشرط يكون كل جزء من المشروط مشروطاً بجزء من الشرط فلا استحالة وأيضاً لا استحالة في تقدم جزء المشروط على الشرط إنما المحال تقدم نفس المشروط على الشرط (وعندهما) يستعار في الطلاق (للإلصاق عوضاً، فينقسم) أجزاء العوض على أجزاء المعوض (فله (الثلث للألف في طلاق واحد (أقول ترجيحهما كما في «التحرير» بأن الأصل فيما علمت مقابلته بمال العوضية) والطلاق مما يقابل بمال، فيحمل فيه على العوضية ضعيف لأن ذلك أي كون العوضية أصلاً (فيما لا يحتمل الشرط المحض أصلاً كالبيع ونحوه، لا في كل ما يقبل المعاوضة في الجملة، هذا وقد يدفع بدعوى الاستقراء والله أعلم ( كترجيحه) أي كما أن ترجيح قول الإمام ضعيف (بأنه) أي على (مجاز في الإلصاق حقيقة في الشرط فيحمل عليه عند إمكانه ( كما ذكره شمس الأئمة) وإنما كان ضعيفاً (لأنه) أي كونه حقيقة في الشرط ممنوع قيل في الاستناد (لأن الإلصاق) المتحقق في العوض حقيقته أي حقيقة على فإنه من أفراد اللزوم) إذ هناك يلزم العوض في الذمة (أقول : اللزوم إنما يتحقق بعد التعلق) الذي يكون في المعاوضة (لأنه يوجب المقابلة، والمقابلة توجب اللزوم فالتعلق يوجب اللزوم والكلام في أصل التعلق) إنه حقيقة فيه أم لا (بعد) فالحق أن الإلصاق والشرطية كلاهما غير اللزوم، فهو فيهما ،مجاز، هذا ومن ادعى أنه حقيقة في الشرط لم يقل بأنه باعتبار اللغة حقيقة، بل يقول : صار في العرف حقيقة، بمعنى لا يحتاج في الانفهام إلى قرينة أصلاً، وهو غير ظاهر الفساد، لكن يلزم عليه البيان (ثم أقول لك أن ترجحه أي قول الإمام بأن تعلق المجموع من الألف (بالمجموع) من الطلقات صوناً عن الإلغاء ضروري سواء كان التعلق شرطياً أو إلصاقياً (وانقسام البعض على البعض زائد بلا دليل فإنه إن كان للشرط فظاهر أنه لا انقسام وإن كان للإلصاق (فإن الطلاق يحتمل الأمرين بعوض المال وبغير عوض المال ولا قيمة له في ذاته أصلاً، حتى يقسم عليها إلا بالشرط والرضا، وقد وقع بتقويم المجموع لا الأجزاء بخلاف البيع ونحوه) فإن للعوضين قيمة في ذاتيهما، فلا بد أن تقع في مقابلة الأجزاء التي هي أموال أجزاء من العوض الآخر وإلاّ لزم بقاء المال بلا عوض، وإذا كان مقابلة الأجزاء بالأجزاء بلا دليل فلم يثبت) . (فرع . في قول رجل له علي ألف يلزم (الدين ويكون إقراراً به لكونه حقيقة في اللزوم وهو كونه ديناً ولو) وصل وديعة تعين (المجاز لوجود الصارف (وهو وجوب الحفظ). ليس ممتداً
Issue: 'ala is for elevation even if metaphorical, i.e., even if the elevation is metaphorical, it generalizes obligation, like debt. It is borrowed in pure commutative contracts, i.e., contracts that are only concluded with exchange of property, like marriage, lease, and sale, for attachment, meaning the preposition 'ba' al-muqabala' by agreement, as in 'carry it for ten', or 'I sold you this slave for ten', or 'I married for ten'. And it is borrowed in divorce for condition, i.e., that what follows is suspended upon what precedes, in his (Abu Hanifa's) view. So in 'divorce me three times for a thousand', he gets nothing for one divorce, i.e., the husband gets nothing for effecting one divorce due to non-division of the conditioned upon the condition. The summary of suspension is that the conditioned is established upon the condition of realization of the condition. But that every part of it is established upon every part of the condition does not follow. If it were established, it would be without cause, so it is not established. Perhaps this is the intent of the one who said that it is divided into parts of the conditioned before the condition; otherwise, it is refuted obviously that as some conditioned exists, some condition exists. So on the assumption of division of parts of the conditioned upon parts of the condition, each part of the conditioned is conditioned by a part of the condition, so there is no impossibility. Also, there is no impossibility in the precedence of part of the conditioned over the condition; the impossible is the precedence of the conditioned itself over the condition. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is borrowed in divorce for attachment as compensation, so it divides parts of the compensation upon parts of the compensated. So he gets a third of the thousand for one divorce. I say: their preference, as in al-Tahrir, that the principle in what is known to be counterbalanced by property is compensation, and divorce is among that which is counterbalanced by property, so it is construed as compensation, is weak because that, i.e., compensation being the principle, is in what does not admit pure condition at all, like sale and similar, not in everything that admits exchange in general. This may be rebutted by claiming induction, and Allah knows best. Like his preference, i.e., that the preference of the Imam's statement is weak, because 'ala is metaphorical in attachment and literal in condition, so it is construed accordingly when possible, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma. It is weak because its being literal in condition is disputed; it was said in support because the attachment realized in compensation is its reality, i.e., the reality of 'ala, for it is a type of obligation, as the compensation is obligated in the liability. I say: obligation is realized only after attachment, which is in exchange, because it necessitates correspondence, and correspondence necessitates obligation. So attachment necessitates obligation, but the discussion is about the origin of attachment: whether it is literal in it or not. After all, the truth is that attachment and conditionality are both other than obligation, so it is metaphorical in both. One who claims it is literal in condition does not say it is literal in language, but says it became literal in custom, meaning it does not need a context to be understood, and this is not obviously corrupt, but it imposes clarification. Then I say you can prefer his, i.e., the Imam's statement, by saying that the attachment of the total of the thousand to the total of the divorces is necessary to avoid nullity, whether the attachment is conditional or compensational. And the division of some upon some is extraneous without evidence. If it is for condition, it is clear there is no division; if it is for attachment, then divorce admits both possibilities: with and without monetary compensation, and it has no value in itself to be divided upon except by condition and consent. It occurs by valuation of the total, not parts, unlike sale and similar, because the two considerations have value in themselves, so they must occur in exchange of parts that are property for parts of the other consideration; otherwise, property would remain without compensation. And if the matching of parts with parts is without evidence, it is not established. (Branch: In a man's saying 'I owe a thousand', the debt is established and it is an acknowledgment because 'ala is literal in obligation, i.e., it being a debt. If he added 'deposit', the figurative meaning is determined due to the presence of the indicator, i.e., the duty of preservation.) It is not extended.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the particle 'ala'. The discussion centers on its meanings in Islamic law. The text explains that 'ala can be used for physical or figurative elevation. In contracts like sale, lease, and marriage, it is used for attachment (ilsaq) similar to the preposition 'ba' for exchange. In divorce, the Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa views it as a condition (shart), meaning the divorce is conditional upon payment, so if only one divorce occurs, the husband gets nothing because the condition (three divorces) is not fulfilled. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) view it as attachment for compensation, meaning it divides the payment proportionally. The author critiques both preferences, siding with Abu Hanifa's reasoning that attaching the total sum to the total divorces avoids nullity, and division of parts is unsupported. The branch (far') applies 'ala's literal meaning of obligation to acknowledgment of debt.

Key Terms
على ('ala): Preposition indicating obligation in debt; when modified by 'deposit', shifts to figurative meaning.
الصارف (al-sarf): Contextual indicator that diverts from literal to figurative meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the branch, what is the legal effect of a person saying 'I have a deposit of $1000 on you' (عليك وديعة ألف)?
A) It is an acknowledgment of debt of $1000.
B) It is an acknowledgment of a deposit of $1000.
C) It is invalid because 'ala cannot be used with deposit.
D) It is ambiguous and requires a judge.

Key Takeaway
With no context, 'ala in 'I owe X' means obligation; adding 'deposit' shifts it to figurative deposit due to the contextual indicator.
